function timeIntegration(app) % choses which script to use for solving the
system
551
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
552
%-----------------
Time integrating
---------------------------%
553
% This script handles the time integration of the rotor impact
554
% depending on the user specified options of impact and modal
reduction
555
%
556
% functions:
557
% ode45() % used if no impact and no modal reduction is chosen
558
% modalgeneral_fun() % is used for no impact with modal reduction
using general EVP approach
559
% modalstand_fun() % is used for no impact with modal reduction using
standard EVP approach
560
% rotorstator_fun() % is used when impact and modal reduction is used
(forced general)
561
%
562
% input:
563
% five structs:
564
% parameters (contains all the user options and the DOFs)
565
% ME (contains the Machine Element parameters)
566
% MAT (contains all the system matrices)
567
% EVP (contains eigenvalues and eigenvectors and eigenfrequencies)
568
% ExperimentalData (contains all the experimental results)
569
% SimulationData (contains the simulation results)
570
%
571
% output:
572
% saved to app.SimulationData struct:
573
% q (the displacement matrix)
574
% q_dot (the velocities matrix)
575
% z (is the full vel.+disp. solution)
576
% t (full time history of the simulation)
577
% te_total (array of times where impact occur)
578
% R (the right eigenvector after reduction)
579
% saved to MAT struct:
580
% A_const ()
581
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
582
583
%------------------------ WITHOUT MODAL REDUCTION
-----------------------%
584
if app.parameters.modal==0
585
if app.parameters.impact == 1
586
disp('impact cannot be calculated without modal reduction')
587
return
588
else
589
end
590
% Initial conditions
591
z0 = zeros(app.parameters.Ndof*2,1);
592
%Y-dir disp
593
z0(1:4:end/2) = z0(1:4:end/2) + 0.001;
594
%Z-dir disp
595
z0(2:4:end/2) = z0(2:4:end/2) + 0.000;
596
%Y-dir vel
597
z0((end/2)+1:4:end) = z0((end/2)+1:4:end) + 0.000;
598
%Z-dir vel
599
z0((end/2)+2:4:end) = z0((end/2)+2:4:end) + 0.2;
600
%Point disp
148
Friction and Normal Force Models for Nonlinear Rotor­Stator Contact Dynamics
==PAGE:159==
601
%z0(app.parameters.Ndof+1) = 0.01;
602
%Point vel
603
z0(1) = z0(1) + 0.0000;
604
%z0(ME.D.dof) = z0(ME.D.dof) + 2;
605
606
tspan = [0 0.1];
607
tic
608
[app.SimulationData.t,z] = ode45(@(t,z) state_int(t,z,app.MAT.
A,app.MAT.M,app.parameters ,app.ME),tspan,z0);
609
toc
610
611
% Extracting data
612
q = z(:,1:end/2).';
613
614
end
615
616
617
%------------------------ WITH MODAL REDUCTION
--------------------------%
618
619
if app.parameters.modal==1 && app.parameters.impact ==0 && strcmp(app.
parameters.EVP,'general')==1
620
[q,app.SimulationData.t]=modalgeneral_fun(app.MAT.Kglob,app.MAT.
Mglob,app.parameters ,app.EVP.eigvecR ,app.EVP.eigvecL ,app.ME);
621
end
622
623
if app.parameters.modal==1 && app.parameters.impact ==0 && strcmp(app.
parameters.EVP,'standard')==1
624
[q,app.SimulationData.t]=modalstand_fun(app.MAT.A,app.parameters ,
app.MAT,app.EVP.eigvecR ,app.EVP.eigvecL ,app.ME);
625
626
end
627
628
%--------------- WITH MODAL REDUCTION AND IMPACT
-------------------------%
629
if app.parameters.modal==1 && app.parameters.impact==1 && strcmp(app.
parameters.EVP,'general')==1
630
% q is the full disp. solution
631
% z is the full vel.+disp. solution
632
% t is the full time history
633
% te_total is the times at event
634
635
[q_dot,q,app.SimulationData.t,app.SimulationData.te_total ,app.
SimulationData.z,app.SimulationData.R,app.MAT.A_const]=
rotorstator_fun(app.MAT.Kglob, ...
636
app.MAT.Mglob,app.parameters ,app.EVP.eigvecR ,app.EVP.eigvecL ,
app.ME,app.ExperimentalData); % does modal reduction and
builds the system based on that and runs time integration
637
end
638
639
% Removing minor imaginary "noise"
640
app.SimulationData.q = real(q);
641
642
if app.parameters.impact==1
643
app.SimulationData.q_dot = real(q_dot);
644
end
645
end

function recalculatingImpactData(app) % recalculates all impact data using
t and z from the ODE solver
648
%% Recalculating impact data
Friction and Normal Force Models for Nonlinear Rotor­Stator Contact Dynamics
149
==PAGE:160==
649
% as the ode solvers uses adaptive timesteps it is not efficient to
extract the
650
% force data inside the ode. This function recalculates the impact
data
651
% from the displacement data found using the ode solvers
652
contact = 0;
653
fieldName = app.parameters.nf_model;
654
fieldNames = {app.parameters.nf_model};
655
%Inidialize
656
app.SimulationData.ImpactData = struct('angle',[zeros(length(app.
SimulationData.z),1)],'indentation',[zeros(length(app.
SimulationData.z),1)],'normalForce',[zeros(length(app.
SimulationData.z),1)],'frictionForce',[zeros(length(app.
SimulationData.z),1)],'gap',[zeros(length(app.SimulationData.z),1)
],'time',[zeros(length(app.SimulationData.z),1)]);
657
658
% calculation loop
659
for i=1:length(app.SimulationData.z)
660
661
if app.parameters.Omegahz == 0
662
angle = deg2rad(app.parameters.chosenHitAngle);
663
else
664
angle = (app.SimulationData.t(i)*app.parameters.Omegahz)*2*pi;
% calculate angle
665
angle = mod(angle, 2*pi); % makes sure the angle is periodic
with 2 Pi
666
end
667
668
z0 = app.SimulationData.z(:,i);
669
z_r = app.SimulationData.R*z0(1:app.parameters.Nr);
670
z_s = z0(app.parameters.Nr+1:end);
671
672
impact_contact_prev = contact;
673
[contact ,gap,alpha,delta,deltad,relVelFriction] = contact_fun(z0,
app.parameters ,app.SimulationData.R,app.ME);
674
impact_contact_pos = contact;
675
676
if impact_contact_prev == 0 && impact_contact_pos ==1
677
imp.contact = contact;
678
imp.gap = gap;
679
imp.alpha = alpha;
680
imp.delta = delta;
681
imp.relImpactVelBefore = deltad;
682
end
683
684
if contact ==1
685
% Calculating indentation normal contact forces
686
F = normalForce_v3(app.parameters.coefficientOfRestitution ,
fieldNames);
687
F.calculateNormalForce(app.ME,imp,alpha,delta,deltad ,
fieldName)
688
Fn = F.Fn;
689
690
Ff = frictionForce(app.SimulationData.t,app.SimulationData.z,
app.parameters ,alpha,app.ME,z_r,z_s,Fn,app.MAT.A_const ,
relVelFriction);
691
Fmu_y = Ff.Fmu_y;
692
Fmu_z = Ff.Fmu_z;
693
694
FrictionVector = [cos(alpha) sin(alpha)
695
-sin(alpha) cos(alpha)] * [Fmu_y ; Fmu_z];
696
150
Friction and Normal Force Models for Nonlinear Rotor­Stator Contact Dynamics
==PAGE:161==
697
else
698
Fn = 0;
699
FrictionVector = [0;0];
700
end
701
% Storing the impact data to a struct
702
app.SimulationData.ImpactData.indentation(i) = delta;
703
app.SimulationData.ImpactData.angle(i) = rad2deg(angle);
704
app.SimulationData.ImpactData.normalForce(i) = Fn;
705
FrictionMagnitude = sqrt(FrictionVector(1)^2+FrictionVector(2)^2);
706
app.SimulationData.ImpactData.frictionForce(i) = FrictionMagnitude
;
707
app.SimulationData.ImpactData.gap(i) = gap;
708
app.SimulationData.ImpactData.time(i) = app.SimulationData.t(i);
709
end
710
end

SimulationData.index_e) * 1000, app.SimulationData.q(

Data Calculation and Extraction
1
function ExperimentalData = extractingExperimentalData_v2(ExperimentalData ,
Sensors)
2
% Force Transducers
3
4
% Averaging the measurments from the two transducers in each direction
5
FTh = mean([-Sensors.FT.east.force;Sensors.FT.west.force]); % Force
measurement in horizontal direction
6
FTv = mean([Sensors.FT.south.force;-Sensors.FT.north.force]); % Force
measurement in vertical direction
7
8
%FTv = mean([FTs;-FTn]); % Force measurement in vertical direction
9
% Mass properties of the housings for inertia calculations
10
m_ih = 1.79 + 44e-3; % Mass of inner housing [kg]
11
m_mh = 8.44 + 44e-3; % Mass of middle housing [kg]
12
13
14
% Calculate contact forces for horizontal and vertical directon.
15
Fch = FTh+m_mh*Sensors.acc.horizontal_middel+m_ih*Sensors.acc.
horizontal_inner; % accounting for the innertia in the horizontal
direction
16
Fcv = FTv+m_ih*Sensors.acc.vertical_inner+m_mh*Sensors.acc.vertical_middel
; % accounting for the innertia in the vertical direction
17
18
19
% combined contact force
20
Fc = [Fch;Fcv];
21
22
% Dynamically written angle!!!
23
alpha = atan2((Sensors.Displacement.z_pos),(Sensors.Displacement.y_pos));
24
25
Fc_cylindrical = zeros(2,length(Sensors.Time));
26
27
% using a transformation matrix to tranform to normal and friction forces
28
for i = 1:length(Sensors.Time)
29
Fc_cylindrical(:,i) = [cos(alpha(i)) sin(alpha(i))
30
-sin(alpha(i)) cos(alpha(i))] * Fc(:,i);
31
end
32
33
% The contact forces for horizontal and vertical direction in cylindrical
34
% coordinates
35
Fcn_cylindrical = Fc_cylindrical(1,:);
36
Fcf_cylindrical = Fc_cylindrical(2,:);
37
38
%Removing positive normal -forces and negative friction forces:
39
Fcn_cylindrical(find(Fcn_cylindrical >0)) = 0;
% Positive values = 0
40
Fcf_cylindrical(find(Fcf_cylindrical <0)) = 0;
% Negative values = 0
41
42
% Remove data when there is no contact
43
if isfield(Sensors ,'Contact') % make sure the contact signal is in use
44
if ~isempty(Sensors.Contact.bool) && max(Sensors.Contact.bool)
45
Fcn_cylindrical(Sensors.Contact.bool == 0) = 0;
46
Fcf_cylindrical(Sensors.Contact.bool == 0) = 0;
Friction and Normal Force Models for Nonlinear Rotor­Stator Contact Dynamics
197
==PAGE:208==
47
end
48
end
49
%Absing values:
50
Fcn_cylindrical = abs(Fcn_cylindrical);
51
Fcf_cylindrical = abs(Fcf_cylindrical);
52
53
ExperimentalData.normalForce = Fcn_cylindrical;
54
ExperimentalData.frictionForce = Fcf_cylindrical;
55
56
%variables
57
forceMeasurementTime = 0.01; % how much of the force data after hit in
seconds
58
forceMeasurementLength = round(forceMeasurementTime*Sensors.samplerate);
59
magnetActivationIndices = ExperimentalData.Magnet.startIndices; % start of
each peak
60
endIndices = ExperimentalData.Magnet.endIndices+Sensors.samplerate; % end
of each peak
61
numberOfTests = numel(magnetActivationIndices); % number of hits done in
test data
62
magnetForce = Sensors.FT.magnet.force; %sensor data on magnet force
63
ExperimentalData.hitAngle = Sensors.angle.data(magnetActivationIndices);
64
peakLengths = endIndices - magnetActivationIndices + 1; % length of each

F.5.4
Contact Function
1
function [contact ,gap,alpha,delta,deltad,tangentialRelVel] = contact_fun(z,par
,eigVecR ,ME)
2
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
3
% This function takes the state vector with initial conditions
4
% (before the ode solver) of the rotor/stator
5
% position and velocity and calculates the gap from this data and
6
% determines if there is contact , it also calculates
7
% the indentation and indentation velocity
8
9
% Input
10
% z: statevector with displacement and position of both rotor and stator
11
% for initial condition
12
% par: parameter struct with DOF information
13
% eigVecR: right eigenvector
14
% ME: a struct with data on the DOF and geometry of the Machine Elements
15
%
16
% Output
17
% contact: is there contact or not (boolean)
18
% gap: shortest distance between rotor and stator
19
% alpha: angle of hit
20
% delta: Indentation
21
% deltad: Indentation velocity
22
%
23
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
24
25
z_r = eigVecR*z(1:par.Nr); % displacement and velocity data for rotor
26
z_s = z(par.Nr+1:end); % displacement and velocity data for stator
27
28
%% Positions/coordinates (p)
29
% Getting the two lateral position of the rotor (in y and z direction)
Friction and Normal Force Models for Nonlinear Rotor­Stator Contact Dynamics
207
==PAGE:218==
30
p_r = [real(z_r(par.Ndof+ME.STAT.dof,1)); real(z_r(par.Ndof+ME.STAT.dof+1,1))
;];
31
% Getting the two lateral position of the stator (in y and z direction)
32
p_s = [real(z_s(1,1)); real(z_s(2,1));];
33
34
%% Velocities (v)
35
% Getting two lateral velocities along the rotor
36
v_r = [real(z_r(ME.STAT.dof,1)); real(z_r(ME.STAT.dof+1,1));];
37
% Getting two lateral velocities along the stator
38
v_s = [real(z_s(5,1)); real(z_s(6,1));];
39
40
41
%% Difference position (d)
42
% Position vector
43
p_d = p_r - p_s;
44
45
% Position vector length
46
p_d_len = sqrt(p_d(1)^2 + p_d(2)^2);
47
48
% Angle of position vector
49
alpha = atan2(p_d(2),p_d(1));
50
51
% Stator geometry
52
[stat_r] = stator_geo_fun(alpha); % radius of the stator
53
54
%% Clearance and contact
55
% Clearance
56
gap = stat_r - (p_d_len + ME.S.rad); % (ME.S.rad is the radius of the shaft
defined in globmat.m)
57
58
%% Difference velocity
59
% Velocity vector
60
v_d = v_r - v_s;
61
% Transformation matrix cartesian into cylindrical
62
transM = [cos(alpha) sin(alpha);
63
-sin(alpha) cos(alpha)];
64
65
% eigVecRotating coordinate system into tangential and radial direction
66
v_d_rn = transM * v_d;
67
68
% Extracting components
69
v_d_n = v_d_rn(1); % Relative velocity in the impact direction
70
v_d_r = v_d_rn(2); % Relative velocity in the tangential direction
71
72
%% Contact properties
73
if gap <= 0
74
contact = 1;
75
else
76
contact = 0;
77
end
78
79
% extracting the indentation and indentation velocity
80
if contact==1
81
delta = -gap; % the indentation
82
deltad = v_d_n; % the indentation velocity
83
tangentialRelVel = v_d_r;
84
else
85
delta = 0;
86
deltad = 0;
87
tangentialRelVel = 0;
88
end

% calculates the hysteresis damping ratio for as many models as
specified in the fieldNames array
127
function calculateHysteresisRatio(ContactForces , cr, fieldNames)
128
for i = 1:length(fieldNames)
129
fieldName = fieldNames{i};
130
% switch case for calculating the hysteresis
131
% damping ratio
132
switch fieldName
133
case 'Safaeifar'
134
ContactForces.hdr.Safaeifar = 5 * (1 - cr) ./ (4 * cr)
;
135
136
case 'HuntCrossley'
137
ContactForces.hdr.HuntCrossley = 3 * (1 - cr) / 2;
138
139
case 'HerbertMcWhannell'
140
ContactForces.hdr.HerbertMcWhannell = 6 * (1 - cr) ./
((2 * cr - 1).^2 + 3);
141
142
case 'LeeWang'
143
ContactForces.hdr.LeeWang = 3 * (1 - cr) / 4;
144
145
case 'Nikravesh'
146
ContactForces.hdr.Nikravesh = 3 * (1 - cr.^2) / 4;
147
148
case 'Gonthier'
149
ContactForces.hdr.Gonthier = (1 - cr.^2) ./ cr;
150
151
case 'ZhiyingQishao'
152
ContactForces.hdr.ZhiyingQishao = 3 * (1 - cr.^2) .*
exp(2 * (1 - cr)) / 4;
Friction and Normal Force Models for Nonlinear Rotor­Stator Contact Dynamics
211
==PAGE:222==
153
154
case 'Flores'
155
ContactForces.hdr.Flores = 8 * (1 - cr) ./ (5 * cr);
156
157
case 'GharibHurmuzlu'
158
ContactForces.hdr.GharibHurmuzlu = 1 ./ cr;
159
160
case 'HuGuo'
161
ContactForces.hdr.HuGuo = 3 * (1 - cr) ./ (2 * cr);
162
163
case 'Yu'
164
hd_r = zeros(length(cr), 1);
165
for j = 1:length(cr)
166
c_r = cr(j);
167
if c_r >= 0 && c_r <= 0.25
168
d = 1;
169
elseif c_r > 0.25 && c_r <= 0.4
170
d = 2.1663 * c_r^3 - 3.7216 * c_r^2 + 0.8724 *
c_r + 0.9409;
171
elseif c_r > 0.4 && c_r <= 0.6
172
d = 1.1664 * c_r^3 - 2.4893 * c_r^2 + 0.3625 *
c_r + 1.0117;
173
elseif c_r > 0.6 && c_r <= 0.8
174
d = 0.5048 * c_r^3 - 1.3255 * c_r^2 - 0.3236 *
c_r + 1.1472;
175
elseif c_r > 0.8 && c_r <= 1
176
d = 0.2256 * c_r^3 - 0.6663 * c_r^2 - 0.8437 *
c_r + 1.2844;
177
else
178
error('Value of cr is out of the defined range
[0, 1]');
179
end
180
hd_r(j) = d / c_r;
181
ContactForces.hdr.Yu = hd_r;
182
end
183
184
otherwise
185
warning('Unknown field name: %s', fieldName);
186
end
187
end
188
end

% calculates the normal force and its two components in y and z
191
function calculateNormalForce(ContactForces ,ME,imp,alpha,delta,deltad ,
fieldName)
192
% Calculate stiffness
193
ContactForces.h_r = (1 - ME.SLE.nu^2)/(ME.SLE.E); % calculating h
for the rotor
194
ContactForces.h_s = (1 - ME.STAT.nu^2)/(ME.STAT.E); % calculating
h for the stator
195
% The stiffness is given (Hetzian contant theory)
196
ContactForces.K = ( 4/(3*(ContactForces.h_r + ContactForces.h_s))
) * ((ME.SLE.outer_radius*ME.STAT.inner_radius)/(ME.SLE.
outer_radius+ME.STAT.inner_radius))^(0.5);
197
198
% Calculate the hysteresis factor
199
ContactForces.chi =
ContactForces.hdr.(fieldName)* ContactForces.
K / abs(imp.relImpactVelBefore); % Assuming deltad^(-) means
the magnitude of deltad
200
201
% Calculate the normal force
212
Friction and Normal Force Models for Nonlinear Rotor­Stator Contact Dynamics
==PAGE:223==
202
ContactForces.Fn = ContactForces.K * delta^ContactForces.n +
ContactForces.chi * delta^ContactForces.n * deltad;
203
204
% Transformation matrix cylindrical to cartesian
205
transM = [cos(-alpha) sin(-alpha);
206
-sin(-alpha) cos(-alpha)];
207
208
% Rotating coordinate system into inertial coordinatesystem
209
Fn_yz = transM * [-ContactForces.Fn 0].';
210
211
% Contact forces in inertial coordinates
212
ContactForces.Fn_y = Fn_yz(1);
213
ContactForces.Fn_z = Fn_yz(2);
214
215
216
end

function F_T = Coulomb(~,Fn,mu_s,mu_k,v)
63
% Check for rolling without slipping
64
if abs(v - 0) < 1e-6 % numerical tolerance
65
F_T = mu_s * Fn;
66
else
67
% Slipping
68
F_T = mu_k*Fn*sign(v);
69
end
70
end
71
function F_T = Ambrosio(~,Fn,mu,v)
72
v_0 = 1e-4;
73
v_1 = 2e-4;
74
%% Calculating c_d
75
if abs(v) < v_0
76
c_d = 0;
77
elseif v_0 <= abs(v) && abs(v) <= v_1
78
c_d = (abs(v)-v_0)/(v_1-v_0);
79
elseif abs(v) < -v_1 || v_1 < abs(v)
80
c_d = 1;
81
end
82
83
F_T = sign(v) * mu * c_d * Fn;
84
85
end
86
function F_T = Benson(~,Fn,mu_s,mu_k,v)
87
c = 50;
88
mu_k = mu_k + (mu_s - mu_k)*exp(-c*abs(v));
89
F_T = Fn * mu_k * sign(v);
90
end

Friction and Normal Force Models for Nonlinear Rotor­Stator Contact Dynamics
==PAGE:225==
92
function F_T = Smooth_Coulomb(~,Fn,mu_k,v)
93
vd = 0.001;
94
F_T = mu_k*Fn*tanh(v/vd);
95
end
96
function F_T = Velocity_Based(~,Fn,mu_s,mu_k,v)
97
% For velocity based
98
B = 0.5; %recomended by Wang 2000
99
E = -2; % recomended by Wang 2000
100
C = 48.275805376740865573403447934514; % calculated
101
vdd = 0.1; %transition velocity
102
Fd = Fn*mu_k;
103
Fs = Fn*mu_s;
104
% Friction force
105
if abs(v) <= vdd
106
F_T = Fs * sin(-C*atan(B*v) + E *(B*v-atan(B*v)));
107
elseif abs(v) > vdd
108
F_T = Fd*sign(v);
109
end
110
end
111
function F_T = Karnopp(~,Fn,mu_s,mu_k,v)
112
Fd = Fn*mu_k;
113
Fs = Fn*mu_s;
114
F_ext = 1;
115
vddd = 0.01;
116
% Friction force
117
if abs(v) <= vddd
118
%F_T = min(Fs,max(F_ext,-Fs)) * sign(v);
119
F_T = Fs*sign(v);
120
elseif abs(v) > vddd
121
F_T = Fd * sign(v);
122
end
123
end
124
function [dz,F_T] = LuGre(~,z,Fn,mu_s,mu_k,v)
125
F_d = mu_k*Fn; % the dynamic friction force
126
F_s = mu_s*Fn; % the static friction force
127
v_Stribeck = 0.001; % stribeck velocity (the velocity at which the
steady -state friction force starts decreasing)
128
gamma = 2; % 2 is a good value (\cite{muvengei2012})
129
sigma_0 = 10^5;
130
sigma_1 = sqrt(10^5);
131
sigma_2 = 0.05;
132
g = F_d + (F_s - F_d) * exp(- (v / v_Stribeck)^gamma);
133
dz = v*(1 - (sigma_0 * z * sign(v) / g));
134
135
F_T = sigma_0 * z + sigma_1 * dz + sigma_2 * v;
136
end
137
end
138
end

Delay Handling Script

function [vertical_middel_alligned ,horizontal_inner_alligned ,

function [Kurtosis ,Skewness ,K,S,mu,sigma,x,y] = calculatingKurtosis(peakHeight
)
2
% Calculates kurtosis and skewness
3
% plots a histogram and writes the statistics on the plot
4

8

15

function [natural_frequency ,spike_amplitude ,f,Y,n] = FFT(t,y)
258
uniform_t = linspace(min(t), max(t), numel(t));
% Uniform time vector
259
uniform_y = interp1(t, y(:,1), uniform_t , 'spline');
% Interpolating the
data
260
261
n = length(uniform_y);
262
tmax = uniform_t(end);
263
samplerate = n/tmax;
264
265
uniform_y = uniform_y - mean(uniform_y);
266
267
Y = fft(uniform_y)/n; % fasst fourrier transform on normal force
268
f = samplerate/n*(0:n-1);
269
270
[peaks] = findpeaks(abs(Y(1:round(n/2))));
222
Friction and Normal Force Models for Nonlinear Rotor­Stator Contact Dynamics
==PAGE:233==
271
spike_amplitude = max(peaks);
272
index = find(abs(Y(1:round(n/2)))==spike_amplitude ,1);
273
natural_frequency = f(index);
274
end

function recalculateForces(oneDOF,t,y,omega,r,R,M,g,mu_s,mu_k,
frictionModel)
27
28
Fn = M*y(:,2).^2*(R-r)+M*g*cos(y(:,1));
29
30
oneDOF.F_g = M*g*sin(y(:,1));
31
32
33
% relative velocity between rotor and stator
34
F_T = zeros(numel(y(:,1)),1);
35
for i = 1:numel(y(:,1))
36
v_rotor = y(i,2)*R+omega*r;
37
v_stator = 0;
38
v=v_stator -v_rotor;
39
switch frictionModel
40
case 'Coulomb'
41
F_T(i) = oneDOF.Coulomb(Fn(i),mu_s,mu_k,v);
42
case 'Ambrosio'
43
F_T(i) = oneDOF.Ambrosio(Fn(i),mu_k,v);
44
case 'Smooth_Coulomb'
45
F_T(i) = oneDOF.Smooth_Coulomb(Fn(i),mu_k,v);
46
case 'Benson'
47
F_T(i) = oneDOF.Benson(Fn(i),mu_s,mu_k,v);
48
case 'Velocity_Based'
Friction and Normal Force Models for Nonlinear Rotor­Stator Contact Dynamics
223
==PAGE:234==
49
F_T(i) = oneDOF.Velocity_Based(Fn(i),mu_s,mu_k,v);
50
case 'Karnopp'
51
F_T(i) = oneDOF.Karnopp(Fn(i),mu_s,mu_k,v);
52
case 'Dahl'
53
[~,F_T(i)] = oneDOF.Dahl(y(i,3),Fn(i),mu_k,v);
54
case 'LuGre'
55
[~,F_T(i)] = oneDOF.LuGre(y(i,3),Fn(i),mu_s,mu_k,v);
56
case 'elastoPlastic'
57
[~,F_T(i)] = oneDOF.elastoPlastic(y(i,3),Fn(i),mu_s,
mu_k,v);
58
end

end

function du = One_DOF_ODE(oneDOF,t, u, omega, mu_s, mu_k, M, r, R, g,I
,frictionModel ,EOM)
67
68
Fn = M*u(2)^2*(R-r)+M*g*cos(u(1));
69
70
du = zeros(3, 1);
71
72
% relative velocity between rotor and stator
73
v_rotor = u(2)*R+omega*r;
74
v_stator = 0;
75
v=v_stator -v_rotor;
76
switch frictionModel
77
case 'Coulomb'
78
F_T = oneDOF.Coulomb(Fn,mu_s,mu_k,v);
79
case 'Ambrosio'
80
F_T = oneDOF.Ambrosio(Fn,mu_k,v);
81
case 'Smooth_Coulomb'
82
F_T = oneDOF.Smooth_Coulomb(Fn,mu_k,v);
83
case 'Benson'
84
F_T = oneDOF.Benson(Fn,mu_s,mu_k,v);
85
case 'Velocity_Based'
86
F_T = oneDOF.Velocity_Based(Fn,mu_s,mu_k,v);
87
case 'Karnopp'
88
F_T = oneDOF.Karnopp(Fn,mu_s,mu_k,v);
89
case 'Dahl'
90
[du(3),F_T] = oneDOF.Dahl(u(3),Fn,mu_k,v);
91
case 'LuGre'
92
[du(3),F_T] = oneDOF.LuGre(u(3),Fn,mu_s,mu_k,v);
93
case 'elastoPlastic'
94
[du(3),F_T] = oneDOF.elastoPlastic(u(3),Fn,mu_s,mu_k,v);
95
end
96
97
du(1) = u(2);
98
switch EOM
99
case 'Newton'
100
du(2) = -g*sin(u(1))/(R-r)+F_T*R/(M*(R-r)^2); % EOM from
Newtons Law
101
case 'Euler'
102
du(2) = (-M*g*sin(u(1))*(R-r)+F_T*R)/I; % EOM from Eulers
law
103
end
104
end

106
function F_T = Coulomb(~,Fn,mu_s,mu_k,v)
224
Friction and Normal Force Models for Nonlinear Rotor­Stator Contact Dynamics
==PAGE:235==
107
% Check for rolling without slipping
108
if abs(v - 0) < 1e-6 % A small threshold to account for numerical
precision
109
% Rolling without slipping condition met
110
F_T = mu_s * Fn;
111
else
112
F_T = mu_k*Fn*sign(v);
113
end
114
end

function F_T = Ambrosio(~,Fn,mu,v)
118
v_0 = 1e-4;
119
v_1 = 2e-4;
120
%% Calculating c_d
121
if abs(v) < v_0
122
c_d = 0;
123
elseif v_0 <= abs(v) && abs(v) <= v_1
124
c_d = (abs(v)-v_0)/(v_1-v_0);
125
elseif abs(v) < -v_1 || v_1 < abs(v)
126
c_d = 1;
127
end
128
F_T = sign(v) * mu * c_d * Fn;
129
end
130
131
function F_T = Benson(~,Fn,mu_s,mu_k,v)
132
c = 50;
133
mu_k = mu_k + (mu_s - mu_k)*exp(-c*abs(v));
134
F_T = Fn * mu_k * sign(v);
135
end
136
137
function F_T = Smooth_Coulomb(~,Fn,mu_k,v)
138
vd = 0.001;
139
F_T = mu_k*Fn*tanh(v/vd);
140
end
141
function F_T = Velocity_Based(~,Fn,mu_s,mu_k,v)
142
% For velocity based
143
B = 0.5; %recomended by Wang 2000
144
E = -2; % recomended by Wang 2000
145
C = 48.275805376740865573403447934514; %calculated (see
velocitybasedfull)
146
vdd = 0.1; %transition velocity
147
Fd = Fn*mu_k;
148
Fs = Fn*mu_s;
149
% Friction force
150
if abs(v) <= vdd
151
F_T = Fs * sin(-C*atan(B*v) + E *(B*v-atan(B*v)));
152
elseif abs(v) > vdd
153
F_T = Fd*sign(v);
154
end
155
end
156
function F_T = Karnopp(~,Fn,mu_s,mu_k,v)
157
Fd = Fn*mu_k;
158
Fs = Fn*mu_s;
159
F_ext = 1;
160
vddd = 0.01;
161
% Friction force
162
if abs(v) <= vddd
163
F_T = min(Fs,max(F_ext,-Fs)) * sign(v);
164
elseif abs(v) > vddd
165
F_T = Fd * sign(v);
166
end
Friction and Normal Force Models for Nonlinear Rotor­Stator Contact Dynamics
225
==PAGE:236==
167
end
168
function [dz,F_T] = Dahl(~,z,Fn,mu_k,v)
169
F_d = mu_k*Fn; % the dynamic friction force
170
alpha = 1;
171
sigma_0 = 10^5;
172
dz = v*(1 - (sigma_0 * z * sign(v)/F_d))^alpha;
173
disp(dz)
174
F_T = sigma_0 * z;
175
end
176
function [dz,F_T] = LuGre(~,z,Fn,mu_s,mu_k,v)
177
F_d = mu_k*Fn; % the dynamic friction force
178
F_s = mu_s*Fn; % the static friction force (find out why it is 1.5
times the dynamic)
179
v_Stribeck = 0.001; % stribeck velocity (the velocity at which the
steady -state friction force starts decreasing)
180
gamma = 2; % 2 is a good value (\cite{muvengei2012})
181
sigma_0 = 10^5;
182
sigma_1 = sqrt(10^5);
183
sigma_2 = 0.05;
184
g = F_d + (F_s - F_d) * exp(- (v / v_Stribeck)^gamma);
185
dz = v*(1 - (sigma_0 * z * sign(v) / g));
186
187
F_T = sigma_0 * z + sigma_1 * dz + sigma_2 * v;
188
end
189
function [dz,F_T] = elastoPlastic(~,z,Fn,mu_s,mu_k,v)
190
F_d = mu_k*Fn; % the dynamic friction force
191
F_s = mu_s*Fn; % the static friction force (find out why it is 1.5
times the dynamic)
192
v_Stribeck = 0.001; % stribeck velocity (the velocity at which the
steady -state friction force starts decreasing)
193
gamma = 2; % 2 is a good value (\cite{muvengei2012})
194
sigma_0 = 10^5;
195
sigma_1 = sqrt(10^5);
196
sigma_2 = 0.05;
197
z_ba = 10^(-6);
198
g = F_d + (F_s - F_d) * exp(- (v / v_Stribeck)^gamma);
199
z_max = g/sigma_0;
200
if abs(z) < z_ba
201
alpha = 0;
202
elseif abs(z) >= z_ba && abs(z) < z_max
203
alpha = (1/2) * (1 + sin(pi * (z - (1/2) * (z_max + z_ba)) / (
z_max - z_ba)));
204
elseif abs(z) >= z_max
205
alpha = 1;
206
end
207
dz = v * (1 - alpha * (sigma_0 * z * sign(v) / g));
208
209
F_T = sigma_0 * z + sigma_1 * dz + sigma_2 * v;
210
end
211
212
end
